<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Manila</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Maynila" and "Maynilad" redirect here. For the Philippine TV series produced by <a href="/wiki/GMA_Network" title="GMA Network">GMA Network</a>, see <a href="/wiki/Maynila_(TV_series)" title="Maynila (TV series)">Maynila (TV series)</a>. For related water companies, see <a href="/wiki/Maynilad_Water_Services" title="Maynilad Water Services">Maynilad Water Services</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manila_Water" title="Manila Water">Manila Water</a>.</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the capital city of the Philippines. For the region, see <a href="/wiki/Metro_Manila" title="Metro Manila">Metro Manila</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Manila_(disambiguation)" title="Manila (disambiguation)">Manila (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Manila</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">Filipino</a>: <span lang="fil"><i>Maynilà</i></span>, <small>pronounced </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Tagalog" title="Help:IPA/Tagalog">[majˈnilaʔ]</a></span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Tagalog" title="Help:IPA/Tagalog">[majniˈla]</a></span>), officially the <b>City of Manila</b> (<a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">Filipino</a>: <span lang="fil"><i>Lungsod ng Maynilà</i></span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Tagalog" title="Help:IPA/Tagalog">[luŋˈsod nɐŋ majˈnilaʔ]</a></span>), is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_population_density" title="List of cities by population density">most densely populated city</a> proper in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arearef1_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-arearef1-3">[3]</a></sup> It was the first chartered City by virtue of the Philippine Commission Act 183 on July 31, 1901 and gained autonomy with the passage of Republic Act No. 409 or the "Revised Charter of the City of Manila" on June 18, 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Spanish City of Manila</a> was founded on June 24, 1571, by <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel López de Legazpi">Miguel López de Legazpi</a>, which was regarded as the official foundation date of the city. Manila was also the seat of power for most of the country's colonial rulers. It is the home to many historic sites, some of which were built during the 16th century. In 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">Globalization and World Cities Research Network</a> listed Manila as an alpha- <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The city proper is home to 1,780,148 people in 2015<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PSA15-NCR_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-PSA15-NCR-6">[6]</a></sup>, and is the historic core of a built-up area that extends well beyond its administrative limits. The term "Manila" is commonly used to refer to the whole metropolitan area, the <a href="/wiki/Mega_Manila" title="Mega Manila">greater metropolitan area</a> or the city proper. The officially-defined metropolitan area called <a href="/wiki/Metro_Manila" title="Metro Manila">Metro Manila</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_region" title="Capital region">capital region</a> of the Philippines, includes the much larger <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Makati_Central_Business_District" title="Makati Central Business District">Makati Central Business District</a>. It is the most populous region of the country, one of the most populous urban areas in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and is one of the wealthiest regions in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> With 71,263 people per square kilometer, Manila is also the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Most_densely_populated_cities" title="Most densely populated cities">most densely populated city</a> proper in the world. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PSA15-NCR_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-PSA15-NCR-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PSApopden_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-PSApopden-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The City of Manila is located on the eastern shores of the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Bay" title="Manila Bay">Manila Bay</a> in one of the finest harbors in the country. The <a href="/wiki/Pasig_River" title="Pasig River">Pasig River</a> flows through the middle of the city, dividing it into the north and south. Manila is made up of 16 districts: <a href="/wiki/Binondo" title="Binondo">Binondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ermita" title="Ermita">Ermita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malate,_Manila" title="Malate, Manila">Malate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paco,_Manila" title="Paco, Manila">Paco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pandacan" title="Pandacan">Pandacan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Area,_Manila" title="Port Area, Manila">Port Area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quiapo,_Manila" title="Quiapo, Manila">Quiapo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sampaloc,_Manila" title="Sampaloc, Manila">Sampaloc</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Andres,_Manila" title="San Andres, Manila">San Andres</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_Manila" title="San Miguel, Manila">San Miguel</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Nicolas,_Manila" title="San Nicolas, Manila">San Nicolas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana,_Manila" title="Santa Ana, Manila">Santa Ana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Manila" title="Santa Cruz, Manila">Santa Cruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mesa" title="Santa Mesa">Santa Mesa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tondo,_Manila" title="Tondo, Manila">Tondo</a>. Manila is also made up of <a href="/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Manila" title="Legislative districts of Manila">Six Congressional Districts</a> that represents the city on the Lower House of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_Philippines" title="Congress of the Philippines">Philippine Congress</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Maynilà</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">Filipino</a> name for the city, originated from the word <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scyphiphora_hydrophyllacea" title="Scyphiphora hydrophyllacea">nilà</a></i>, referring to a flowering <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangrove tree</a> that grew on the delta of the <a href="/wiki/Pasig_River" title="Pasig River">Pasig River</a> and the shores of <a href="/wiki/Manila_Bay" title="Manila Bay">Manila Bay</a>. The flowers were made into garlands that, according to folklore, were offered to statues on religious altars or in churches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> As <i>nilà</i> products were distributed in other places, people came to refer to the area as <i>Sa may Nilà</i>, <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a> for "the place where there are <i>nilàs</i>". The word <i>nilà</i> itself is probably from the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> <i>nila</i> (नील), meaning "indigo tree".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-E.M._Pospelov.2C_1998_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-E.M._Pospelov.2C_1998-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Manila" title="History of Manila">History of Manila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Manila" title="Timeline of Manila">Timeline of Manila</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Precolonial_history">Precolonial history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Precolonial history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="355" data-file-width="600" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription.gif/220px-Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription.gif/330px-Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription.gif/440px-Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Laguna_Copperplate_Inscription" title="Laguna Copperplate Inscription">Laguna Copperplate Inscription</a> is the oldest historical record in the Philippines. It has the first historical reference to <a href="/wiki/Tondo_(historical_polity)" title="Tondo (historical polity)">Tondo</a> and dates back to <a href="/wiki/Shaka_era" title="Shaka era">Saka</a> 822 (c. 900).</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MalateManilajf9508_07.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/MalateManilajf9508_07.JPG/220px-MalateManilajf9508_07.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/MalateManilajf9508_07.JPG/330px-MalateManilajf9508_07.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/MalateManilajf9508_07.JPG/440px-MalateManilajf9508_07.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MalateManilajf9508_07.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rajah_Sulayman" title="Rajah Sulayman">Rajah Sulayman</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The earliest evidence of human life around present-day Manila is the nearby <a href="/wiki/Angono_Petroglyphs" title="Angono Petroglyphs">Angono Petroglyphs</a>, dated to around 3000 BC. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negritos" title="Negritos">Negritos</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australoid" title="Australoid">Australoid</a> people who became the aboriginal inhabitants of the Philippines, lived across the island of <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>, where Manila is located, before the <a href="/wiki/Malayo-Polynesian_languages" title="Malayo-Polynesian languages">Malayo-Polynesians</a> migrated in and assimilated them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The polity of <a href="/wiki/Tondo_(historical_polity)" title="Tondo (historical polity)">Tondo</a> flourished during the latter half of the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> as a result of direct trade relations with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. The Tondo district was the traditional capital of the empire, and its rulers were sovereign kings, not mere chieftains. They were addressed variously as <i>panginuan</i> in <a href="/wiki/Maranao_language" title="Maranao language">Maranao</a> or <i>panginoón</i> in Tagalog ("lords"); <i>anák banwa</i> ("son of heaven"); or <i><a href="/wiki/Lakandula" title="Lakandula">lakandula</a></i> ("lord of the palace"). The <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_China" title="Emperor of China">Emperor of China</a> considered the <a href="/wiki/Lakan" title="Lakan">Lakans</a>—the rulers of ancient Manila—"王", or kings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManilaHistoryJSTOR_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ManilaHistoryJSTOR-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 13th century, Manila consisted of a fortified settlement and trading quarter on the shore of the Pasig River. It was then settled by the <a href="/wiki/Greater_India" title="Greater India">Indianized</a> empire of <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a>, as recorded in the epic eulogy poem "<a href="/wiki/Nagarakretagama" title="Nagarakretagama">Nagarakretagama</a>", which described the area's conquest by <a href="/wiki/Maharaja" title="Maharaja">Maharaja</a> <a href="/wiki/Hayam_Wuruk" title="Hayam Wuruk">Hayam Wuruk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManilaHistoryJSTOR_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-ManilaHistoryJSTOR-17">[17]</a></sup> Selurong (षेलुरोन्ग्), a historical name for Manila, is listed in Canto 14 alongside Sulot, which is now <a href="/wiki/Sulu" title="Sulu">Sulu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kalka" title="Kalka">Kalka</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManilaHistoryJSTOR_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-ManilaHistoryJSTOR-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the reign of <a href="/wiki/Bolkiah" title="Bolkiah">Sultan Bolkiah</a> from 1485 to 1521, the <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">Sultanate of Brunei</a> invaded, wanting to take advantage of Tondo's trade with China by attacking its environs and establishing the Muslim <a href="/wiki/Rajahnate_of_Maynila" title="Rajahnate of Maynila">Rajahnate of Maynilà</a> (كوتا سلودوڠ; <i>Kota Seludong</i>). The rajahnate was ruled under and gave yearly tribute to the Sultanate of Brunei as a <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">satellite state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pusat_Sejarah_Brunei2_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pusat_Sejarah_Brunei2-18">[18]</a></sup> It established a new dynasty under the local leader, who accepted <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajah_Sulaiman_I" title="Rajah Sulaiman I">Rajah Salalila or Sulaiman I</a>. He established a trading challenge to the already rich <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lakan_Dula" title="Lakan Dula">House of Lakan Dula</a> in Tondo. Islam was further strengthened by the arrival of Muslim traders from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In 1574, Manila was temporarily besieged by the Chinese pirate <a href="/wiki/Lim_Hong" title="Lim Hong">Lim Hong</a>, who was ultimately thwarted by the local inhabitants. The city then became the seat of the Spanish colonial government.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_period">Spanish period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Spanish period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="892" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg/220px-Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg/330px-Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg/440px-Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Cathedral_before_the_1880_earthquake.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The newly rebuilt <a href="/wiki/Manila_Cathedral" title="Manila Cathedral">Manila Cathedral</a> in 1880 before the earthquake of July 20, 1880, which knocked down the over-a-century old bell tower.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On June 24, 1571, the conquistador <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel López de Legazpi">Miguel López de Legazpi</a> arrived in Manila and declared it a territory of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>, establishing a city council in what is now the district of <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> López de Legazpi had the local royalty executed or exiled after the failure of the <a href="/wiki/Tondo_Conspiracy" title="Tondo Conspiracy">Tondo Conspiracy</a>, a plot wherein an alliance between <a href="/wiki/Datu" title="Datu">datus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raja" title="Raja">rajahs</a>, Japanese merchants and the <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">Sultanate of Brunei</a> would band together to execute the Spaniards, along with their <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Asian" title="Latin American Asian">Latin American</a> recruits and Visayan allies. The victorious Spaniards made Manila, the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a> and of the Philippines, which their empire would control for the next three centuries.</p>
<p>Manila became famous during the <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Manila–Acapulco galleon</a> trade, which lasted for three centuries and brought goods from <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and Hispanic America across the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Islands</a> to Southeast Asia (which was already an <a href="/wiki/Entrep%C3%B4t" title="Entrepôt">entrepôt</a> for goods coming from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and China), and vice versa. <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">Silver</a> that was mined in Mexico and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> was exchanged for Chinese <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">silk</a>, Indian gems and the spices of Southeast Asia. Likewise, <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a> grown in Europe and North Africa were shipped via Mexico to Manila.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kane_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kane-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1762)" title="Battle of Manila (1762)">The city was captured</a> by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> in 1762 as part of the European <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> between Spain, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a> and Great Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/British_occupation_of_Manila" title="British occupation of Manila">city was then occpuied</a> by the British for almost two years from 1762 to 1764 and remained the capital of the Philippines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Backhouse_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Backhouse-23">[23]</a></sup> Eventually, the British withdrew in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">1763 Treaty of Paris</a>. An unknown number of Indian soldiers known as <a href="/wiki/Sepoy" title="Sepoy">sepoys</a>, who came with the British, deserted and settled in nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cainta,_Rizal" title="Cainta, Rizal">Cainta, Rizal</a>, which explains the uniquely Indian features of generations of Cainta residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Chinese were then punished for supporting the British invasion, and the fortress city of <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a>, initially populated by 1200 Spanish families and garrisoned by 400 Spanish troops,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> kept its cannons pointed at <a href="/wiki/Binondo" title="Binondo">Binondo</a>, the world's oldest <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinatown</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-en.radio86.com_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-en.radio86.com-27">[27]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Asian" title="Latin American Asian">Mexican</a> population was concentrated at the south part of Manila,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and also at <a href="/wiki/Cavite_City" title="Cavite City">Cavite</a>, where ships from Spain's American colonies docked, and at <a href="/wiki/Ermita" title="Ermita">Ermita</a>, an area so named because of a Mexican hermit that lived there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexico gained independence</a> in 1821, Spain began to govern Manila directly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Under direct Spanish rule, banking, industry and education flourished more than they had in the previous two centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The opening of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> in 1869 facilitated direct trade and communications with Spain. The city's growing wealth and education attracted indigenous people, Chinese, Indians, Latinos, and Europeans from the surrounding provinces<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a112_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-a112-33">[33]</a></sup> and facilitated the rise of an <i><a href="/wiki/Ilustrado" title="Ilustrado">ilustrado</a></i> class that espoused <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> ideas: the ideological foundations of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">Philippine Revolution</a>, which sought independence from Spain.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_period">American period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: American period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manilastreetcar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="679" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Manilastreetcar.jpg/220px-Manilastreetcar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Manilastreetcar.jpg/330px-Manilastreetcar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Manilastreetcar.jpg/440px-Manilastreetcar.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manilastreetcar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">Tram</a> running along Manila during the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)" title="History of the Philippines (1898–1946)">American period</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1898)" title="Battle of Manila (1898)">1898 Battle of Manila</a>, Spain ceded Manila to the United States. The <a href="/wiki/First_Philippine_Republic" title="First Philippine Republic">First Philippine Republic</a>, based in nearby <a href="/wiki/Bulacan" title="Bulacan">Bulacan</a>, fought against the Americans for control of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The Americans defeated the First Philippine Republic and captured President <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Aguinaldo" title="Emilio Aguinaldo">Emilio Aguinaldo</a>, who declared allegiance to the United States on April 1, 1901.</p>
<p>Upon drafting a new charter for Manila in June 1901, the Americans made official what had long been tacit: that the city of Manila consisted not of Intramuros alone but also of the surrounding areas. The new charter proclaimed that Manila was composed of eleven municipal districts: presumably Binondo, <a href="/wiki/Ermita" title="Ermita">Ermita</a>, Intramuros, <a href="/wiki/Malate,_Manila" title="Malate, Manila">Malate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paco,_Manila" title="Paco, Manila">Paco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pandacan" title="Pandacan">Pandacan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sampaloc,_Manila" title="Sampaloc, Manila">Sampaloc</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_Manila" title="San Miguel, Manila">San Miguel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana,_Manila" title="Santa Ana, Manila">Santa Ana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Manila" title="Santa Cruz, Manila">Santa Cruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tondo,_Manila" title="Tondo, Manila">Tondo</a>. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> recognized five parishes—Gagalangin, Trozo, Balic-Balic, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mesa" title="Santa Mesa">Santa Mesa</a> and Singalong—as part of Manila. Later, two more would be added: Balut and <a href="/wiki/San_Andres,_Manila" title="San Andres, Manila">San Andres</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JN_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-JN-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BurnhamPlanOf-Manila.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1088" data-file-width="1328" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/BurnhamPlanOf-Manila.jpg/220px-BurnhamPlanOf-Manila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/BurnhamPlanOf-Manila.jpg/330px-BurnhamPlanOf-Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/BurnhamPlanOf-Manila.jpg/440px-BurnhamPlanOf-Manila.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BurnhamPlanOf-Manila.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Burnham" title="Daniel Burnham">Burnham Plan</a> of Manila.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under American control, a new, civilian-oriented <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insular_Government" title="Insular Government">Insular Government</a> headed by <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Philippines" title="Governor-General of the Philippines">Governor-General</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a> invited city planner <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Burnham" title="Daniel Burnham">Daniel Burnham</a> to adapt Manila to modern needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The Burnham Plan included the development of a road system, the use of waterways for transportation, and the beautification of Manila with waterfront improvements and construction of parks, parkways and buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>The planned buildings included a government center occupying all of Wallace Field, which extends from <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Park" title="Rizal Park">Rizal Park</a> to the present <a href="/wiki/Taft_Avenue" title="Taft Avenue">Taft Avenue</a>. The Philippine Capitol was to rise at the Taft Avenue end of the field, facing toward the sea. Along with buildings for various government bureaus and departments, it would form a quadrangle with a <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">lagoon</a> in the center and a monument to <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal" title="José Rizal">José Rizal</a> at the other end of the field. Of Burnham's proposed government center, only three units—the Legislative Building and the buildings of the Finance and Agricultural Departments—were completed when <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> erupted.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japanese_occupation_and_World_War_II">Japanese occupation and World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Japanese occupation and World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Walled_City_Destruction_May_1945.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="959" data-file-width="1600" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Manila_Walled_City_Destruction_May_1945.jpg/220px-Manila_Walled_City_Destruction_May_1945.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Manila_Walled_City_Destruction_May_1945.jpg/330px-Manila_Walled_City_Destruction_May_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Manila_Walled_City_Destruction_May_1945.jpg/440px-Manila_Walled_City_Destruction_May_1945.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Walled_City_Destruction_May_1945.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The destruction brought about by the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1945)" title="Battle of Manila (1945)">Battle of Manila</a> in 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Philippines" title="Japanese occupation of the Philippines">Japanese occupation of the Philippines</a>, American soldiers were ordered to withdraw from Manila, and all military installations were removed on December 24, 1941. General <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">Douglas MacArthur</a> declared Manila an <a href="/wiki/Open_city" title="Open city">open city</a> to prevent further death and destruction, but Japanese warplanes continued to bomb it. Manila was occupied by <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese forces</a> on January 2, 1942.</p>
<p>From February 3 to March 3, 1945, Manila was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1945)" title="Battle of Manila (1945)">bloodiest battle</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific theater</a> of World War II. Some <a href="/wiki/Manila_massacre" title="Manila massacre">100,000 civilians were killed</a> in February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> At the end of the battle, Manila was recaptured by joint American and Philippine troops. It was the second most devastated city in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, during the Second World War. Almost all of the structures in the city, particularly in Intramuros, were destroyed.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_period">Contemporary period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Contemporary period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avenida_in_Rizal,_Manila_in_the_mid_90%27s.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="850" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Avenida_in_Rizal%2C_Manila_in_the_mid_90%27s.jpg/220px-Avenida_in_Rizal%2C_Manila_in_the_mid_90%27s.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Avenida_in_Rizal%2C_Manila_in_the_mid_90%27s.jpg/330px-Avenida_in_Rizal%2C_Manila_in_the_mid_90%27s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Avenida_in_Rizal%2C_Manila_in_the_mid_90%27s.jpg/440px-Avenida_in_Rizal%2C_Manila_in_the_mid_90%27s.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avenida_in_Rizal,_Manila_in_the_mid_90%27s.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rizal_Avenue" title="Rizal Avenue">Rizal Avenue</a> in the 1970s before the construction of <a href="/wiki/Manila_Light_Rail_Transit_System_Line_1" title="Manila Light Rail Transit System Line 1">LRT Line 1</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1948, President <a href="/wiki/Elpidio_Quirino" title="Elpidio Quirino">Elpidio Quirino</a> moved the seat of government of the Philippines to <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a>, a new capital in the suburbs and fields northeast of Manila, created in 1939 during the administration of President <a href="/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon" title="Manuel L. Quezon">Manuel L. Quezon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The move ended any implementation of the Burnham Plan's intent for the government centre to be at Luneta.</p>
<p>With the Visayan-born <a href="/wiki/Arsenio_Lacson" title="Arsenio Lacson">Arsenio Lacson</a> as its first elected <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Manila" title="Mayor of Manila">mayor</a> in 1952 (all mayors were appointed before this), Manila underwent <i>The Golden Age</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RoseHistorianManila_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-RoseHistorianManila-41">[41]</a></sup> once again earning its status as the "Pearl of the Orient", a moniker it earned before the Second World War. After Lacson's term in the 1950s, Manila was led by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Villegas" title="Antonio Villegas">Antonio Villegas</a> for most of the 1960s. <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Bagatsing" title="Ramon Bagatsing">Ramon Bagatsing</a> (an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian-Filipino" title="Indian-Filipino">Indian-Filipino</a>) was mayor for nearly the entire 1970s until the 1986 <a href="/wiki/People_Power_Revolution" title="People Power Revolution">People Power Revolution</a>. Mayors Lacson, Villegas, and Bagatsing are collectively known as the "Big Three of Manila" for their contribution to the development of the city and their lasting legacy in improving the quality of life and welfare of the people of Manila.</p>
<p>During the administration of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Marcos" title="Ferdinand Marcos">Ferdinand Marcos</a>, the region of Metro Manila was created as an integrated unit with the enactment of Presidential Decree No. 824 on November 7, 1975. The area encompassed four <a href="/wiki/Cities_of_the_Philippines" title="Cities of the Philippines">cities</a> and thirteen adjoining <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Philippines" title="Municipalities of the Philippines">towns</a>, as a separate regional unit of government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> On the 405th anniversary of the city's foundation on June 24, 1976, Manila was reinstated by Marcos as the capital of the Philippines for its historical significance as the seat of government since the Spanish Period. Presidential Decree No. 940 states that Manila has always been to the Filipino people and in the eyes of the world, the premier city of the Philippines being the center of trade, commerce, education and culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Martial_law_in_the_Philippines" title="Martial law in the Philippines">martial law era</a>, Manila became a hot-bed of resistance activity as youth and student demonstrators repeatedly clashed with the police and military which were subservient to the Marcos regime. After decades of resistance, the non-violent <a href="/wiki/People_Power_Revolution" title="People Power Revolution">People Power Revolution</a> (predecessor to the peaceful-revolutions that <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">toppled the iron-curtain in Europe</a>), ousted the authoritarian Marcos from power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1992, <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Lim" title="Alfredo Lim">Alfredo Lim</a> was elected mayor, the first <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Filipino" title="Chinese Filipino">Chinese-Filipino</a> to hold the office. He was known for his anti-crime crusades. Lim was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Lito_Atienza" title="Lito Atienza">Lito Atienza</a>, who served as his vice mayor. Atienza was known for his campaign (and city slogan) "<i>Buhayin ang Maynila</i>" (<i>Revive Manila</i>), which saw the establishment of several parks and the repair and rehabilitation of the city's deteriorating facilities. He was the city's mayor for 3 terms (9 years) before being termed out of office.</p>
<p>Lim once again ran for mayor and defeated Atienza's son Ali in the 2007 city election and immediately reversed all of Atienza's projects<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> claiming Atienza's projects made little contribution to the improvements of the city. The relationship of both parties turned bitter, with the two pitting again during the <a href="/wiki/Manila_local_elections,_2010" title="Manila local elections, 2010">2010 city elections</a> in which Lim won against Atienza.</p>
<p>Lim was sued by councilor Dennis Alcoreza on 2008 over <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> charged with <a href="/wiki/Graft_(politics)" title="Graft (politics)">graft</a> over the rehabilitation of public schools,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and was heavily criticized for his haphazard resolution of the <a href="/wiki/Manila_hostage_crisis" title="Manila hostage crisis">Rizal Park hostage taking incident</a>, one of the deadliest hostage crisis in the Philippines. Later on, Vice Mayor <a href="/wiki/Isko_Moreno" title="Isko Moreno">Isko Moreno</a> and 28 city councilors filed another case against Lim in 2012, stating that Lim's statement in a meeting were "life-threatening" to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:119th_Rizal_Day_commemoration.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="487" data-file-width="800" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/119th_Rizal_Day_commemoration.jpg/220px-119th_Rizal_Day_commemoration.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/119th_Rizal_Day_commemoration.jpg/330px-119th_Rizal_Day_commemoration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/119th_Rizal_Day_commemoration.jpg/440px-119th_Rizal_Day_commemoration.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:119th_Rizal_Day_commemoration.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 119th commemoration of Rizal Day at the <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Park" title="Rizal Park">Rizal Park</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Torre_de_Manila_controversy" title="Torre de Manila controversy">controversial</a> <a href="/wiki/Torre_de_Manila" title="Torre de Manila">Torre de Manila</a> in the background.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2012, <a href="/wiki/DMCI_Homes" title="DMCI Homes">DMCI Homes</a> began constructing <a href="/wiki/Torre_de_Manila" title="Torre de Manila">Torre de Manila</a>, which became controversial for <a href="/wiki/Visual_pollution" title="Visual pollution">ruining the sight line</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Park" title="Rizal Park">Rizal Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> It is infamously known as the "national photobomber" or as "Terror de Manila".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Torre_de_Manila_controversy" title="Torre de Manila controversy">Torre de Manila controversy</a> is regarded as one of the most sensationalized heritage issues of the country.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Manila_local_elections,_2013" title="Manila local elections, 2013">2013 elections</a>, former President <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Estrada" title="Joseph Estrada">Joseph Estrada</a> defeated Lim in the mayoral race. During his term, Estrada has paid more than ₱5 billion in city debts and increased the city's revenues from ₱6.2 billion in 2012 to ₱14.6 billion by 2016, resulting in increased infrastructure spending and the betterment of the welfare of the people of Manila.</p>
<p>In 2015, the city became the most competitive city in the Philippines, making the city the best place for doing business and for living in. However, despite these achievements, Estrada only narrowly won over Lim in their electoral rematch in <a href="/wiki/Manila_local_elections,_2016" title="Manila local elections, 2016">2016</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Recently, the City Government is planning to revise existing curfew ordinance since the Supreme Court declared it unconstitutional on August 2017. Out of the three cities reviewed by the Supreme Court, namely: the City of Manila, <a href="/wiki/Navotas" title="Navotas">Navotas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a>; only the curfew ordinance of Quezon City was approved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Manila" title="Geography of Manila">Geography of Manila</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Bay_Sunset_(2).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Manila_Bay_Sunset_%282%29.JPG/220px-Manila_Bay_Sunset_%282%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Manila_Bay_Sunset_%282%29.JPG/330px-Manila_Bay_Sunset_%282%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Manila_Bay_Sunset_%282%29.JPG/440px-Manila_Bay_Sunset_%282%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Bay_Sunset_(2).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The iconic <a href="/wiki/Manila_Bay" title="Manila Bay">Manila Bay</a> sunset</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iss047e099713_lrg_Manila.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3280" data-file-width="4928" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Iss047e099713_lrg_Manila.jpg/220px-Iss047e099713_lrg_Manila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Iss047e099713_lrg_Manila.jpg/330px-Iss047e099713_lrg_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Iss047e099713_lrg_Manila.jpg/440px-Iss047e099713_lrg_Manila.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iss047e099713_lrg_Manila.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">ISS</a> photo of Manila (just left of center) and surrounding cities</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The City of Manila is situated on the eastern shore of <a href="/wiki/Manila_Bay" title="Manila Bay">Manila Bay</a>, on the western edge of <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>, 1300 km from mainland <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> One of Manila's greatest natural resources is the protected harbor upon which it sits, regarded as the finest in all of Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pasig_River" title="Pasig River">Pasig River</a> flows through the middle of city, dividing it into the north and south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arearef1_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-arearef1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arearef2_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-arearef2-4">[4]</a></sup> The overall <a href="/wiki/Grading_(engineering)" title="Grading (engineering)">grade</a> of the city's central, built-up areas, is relatively consistent with the natural flatness of its overall natural geography, generally exhibiting only slight differentiation otherwise.</p>
<p>Almost all of Manila sits on top of centuries of prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Alluvium" title="Alluvium">alluvial</a> deposits built by the waters of the Pasig River and on some land reclaimed from Manila Bay. Manila's land has been altered substantially by human intervention, with considerable <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a> along the waterfronts since the American colonial times. Some of the city's natural variations in topography have been evened out. As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Manila had a total area of 42.88 square kilometers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arearef1_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-arearef1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arearef2_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-arearef2-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2017, the City Government approved five reclamation projects: the New Manila Bay International Community (407.43 hectares), Solar City (148 hectares), the Manila Harbour Center expansion (50 hectares), Manila Waterfront City (318 hectares)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and Horizon Manila (419 hectares). Once completed, it will increase the city's total area from 42.88 km<sup>2</sup> (4,288 ha) to 58.3 km<sup>2</sup> (5,830 ha). Projects such as these have been criticized by environmentalists and the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, stating that these reclamation projects are not sustainable and would put communities at risk of flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Another reclamation project is possible and when built, it will contain the in-city housing relocation projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes">Earthquakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Earthquakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_the_Philippines" title="List of earthquakes in the Philippines">List of earthquakes in the Philippines</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Swiss_Re" title="Swiss Re">Swiss Re</a>, the world’s second-largest reinsurer based in <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, places Manila as the second riskiest capital city to live in. The company cited dangers of earthquakes and flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The seismically active <a href="/wiki/Marikina_Valley_Fault_System" title="Marikina Valley Fault System">Marikina Valley Fault System</a> poses a threat to Manila and the surrounding regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Manila has endured several deadly earthquakes, notably in <a href="/wiki/1645_Luzon_earthquake" title="1645 Luzon earthquake">1645</a> and in 1677 which destroyed the stone and brick medieval city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earthquake_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Earthquake-62">[62]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Earthquake_Baroque" title="Earthquake Baroque">Earthquake Baroque</a> style was used by architects during the Spanish colonial period in order to adapt to the frequent earthquakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-City_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-City-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> system, Manila has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna climate</a> (Köppen climate classification Aw). Together with the rest of the Philippines, Manila lies entirely within the tropics. Its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> means that the temperature range is very small, rarely going below 20°C or above 38°C. Temperature extremes have ranged from 14.5°C on January 11, 1914,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> to 38.6°C on May 7, 1915.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humidity levels are usually very high all year round. Manila has a distinct <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a> from December through May, and a relatively lengthy <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> that covers the remaining period with slightly cooler temperatures. In the wet season, it rarely rains all day, but rainfall is very heavy during short periods. <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">Typhoons</a> usually occur from June to September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Due to industrial waste and automobiles, Manila suffers from <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNcyberbus_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNcyberbus-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> affecting 98% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Annually, the air pollution causes more than 4,000 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Ermita is Manila's most air polluted district due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_dump" title="Open dump">open dump sites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_waste" title="Industrial waste">industrial waste</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PollutionManila_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-PollutionManila-73">[73]</a></sup> According to a report in 2003, the Pasig River is one of the most polluted rivers in the world with 150 tons of domestic waste and 75 tons of industrial waste dumped daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Annually, Manila is hit with 5 to 7 typhoons creating floods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AOML_FAQ_B2_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-AOML_FAQ_B2-75">[75]</a></sup> In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Ketsana" title="Typhoon Ketsana">Typhoon Ketsana (Ondoy)</a> struck the Philippines. In its aftermath, the lack of infrastructure led to one of the worst floodings in the Philippines and creating a significant amount of pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ondoy_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ondoy-76">[76]</a></sup> Following the aftermath of Typhoon Ketsana, the city began to dredge its rivers and improve its drainage network. The <a href="/wiki/Pasig_River_Rehabilitation_Commission" title="Pasig River Rehabilitation Commission">Pasig River Rehabilitation Commission</a> is in charge of cleaning up the Pasig River and <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a> for transportation, recreation and tourism purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PD274_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-PD274-77">[77]</a></sup> Rehabilitation efforts have resulted in the creation of parks along the riverside, along with stricter pollution controls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pianews_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-pianews-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:958px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Big_Manila.jpg" title="The bay skyline of Manila as seen from Harbour Square."><img alt="" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="2040" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Big_Manila.jpg/950px-Big_Manila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Big_Manila.jpg/1425px-Big_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Big_Manila.jpg/1900px-Big_Manila.jpg 2x" width="950"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Big_Manila.jpg" title="File:Big Manila.jpg"></a></div>
The bay skyline of Manila as seen from Harbour Square.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city is made up of fourteen city districts, according to Republic Act No. 409—the Revised Charter of the City of Manila—the basis of which officially sets the present-day boundary of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Two were later added, which are <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mesa" title="Santa Mesa">Santa Mesa</a> (partitioned off from Sampaloc) and <a href="/wiki/San_Andres,_Manila" title="San Andres, Manila">San Andres</a> (partitioned off from Santa Ana).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luneta_Hotel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4608" data-file-width="3456" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Luneta_Hotel.jpg/220px-Luneta_Hotel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Luneta_Hotel.jpg/330px-Luneta_Hotel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Luneta_Hotel.jpg/440px-Luneta_Hotel.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luneta_Hotel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Luneta_Hotel" title="Luneta Hotel">Luneta Hotel</a>, an example of <a href="/wiki/French_Renaissance_architecture" title="French Renaissance architecture">French Renaissance architecture</a> with Filipino stylized beaux art</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Metropolitan_Theater_or_commonly_called_the_Met,_an_abandoned_art_deco_building_in_the_heart_of_Manila.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2313" data-file-width="3726" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Manila_Metropolitan_Theater_or_commonly_called_the_Met%2C_an_abandoned_art_deco_building_in_the_heart_of_Manila.jpg/220px-Manila_Metropolitan_Theater_or_commonly_called_the_Met%2C_an_abandoned_art_deco_building_in_the_heart_of_Manila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Manila_Metropolitan_Theater_or_commonly_called_the_Met%2C_an_abandoned_art_deco_building_in_the_heart_of_Manila.jpg/330px-Manila_Metropolitan_Theater_or_commonly_called_the_Met%2C_an_abandoned_art_deco_building_in_the_heart_of_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Manila_Metropolitan_Theater_or_commonly_called_the_Met%2C_an_abandoned_art_deco_building_in_the_heart_of_Manila.jpg/440px-Manila_Metropolitan_Theater_or_commonly_called_the_Met%2C_an_abandoned_art_deco_building_in_the_heart_of_Manila.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Metropolitan_Theater_or_commonly_called_the_Met,_an_abandoned_art_deco_building_in_the_heart_of_Manila.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The façade of the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Metropolitan_Theater" title="Manila Metropolitan Theater">Manila Metropolitan Theater</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Juan_M._Arellano" title="Juan M. Arellano">Juan M. Arellano</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:0151jfSanta_Cruz_Recto_Avenue_Binondo_Streets_Manilafvf_05.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/0151jfSanta_Cruz_Recto_Avenue_Binondo_Streets_Manilafvf_05.JPG/220px-0151jfSanta_Cruz_Recto_Avenue_Binondo_Streets_Manilafvf_05.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/0151jfSanta_Cruz_Recto_Avenue_Binondo_Streets_Manilafvf_05.JPG/330px-0151jfSanta_Cruz_Recto_Avenue_Binondo_Streets_Manilafvf_05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/0151jfSanta_Cruz_Recto_Avenue_Binondo_Streets_Manilafvf_05.JPG/440px-0151jfSanta_Cruz_Recto_Avenue_Binondo_Streets_Manilafvf_05.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:0151jfSanta_Cruz_Recto_Avenue_Binondo_Streets_Manilafvf_05.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The façade of the <a href="/wiki/Natividad_Building" title="Natividad Building">Natividad Building</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Manila is known for its eclectic mix of architecture that shows a wide range of styles spanning different historical and cultural periods. Architectural styles reflect American, Spanish, Chinese, and Malay influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Prominent Filipino architects such as Antonio Toledo, Felipe Roxas, <a href="/wiki/Juan_M._Arellano" title="Juan M. Arellano">Juan M. Arellano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Map%C3%BAa" title="Tomás Mapúa">Tomás Mapúa</a> have designed significant buildings in Manila such as churches, government offices, theaters, mansions, schools and universities.</p>
<p>Manila is also famed for its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_Deco_theaters_of_Manila" title="Art Deco theaters of Manila">Art Deco theaters</a>. Some of these were designed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Artists_of_the_Philippines" title="National Artists of the Philippines">National Artists for Architecture</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Juan_Nakpil" title="Juan Nakpil">Juan Nakpil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Antonio" title="Pablo Antonio">Pablo Antonio</a>. Unfortunately most of these theaters were neglected, and some of it have been demolished. The historic <a href="/wiki/Escolta_Street" title="Escolta Street">Escolta Street</a> in Binondo features many buildings of <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beaux-Arts_architecture" title="Beaux-Arts architecture">Beaux-Arts</a> architectural style, many of which were designed by prominent Filipino architects during the American Rule in the 1920s to the late 1930s. Many architects, artists, historians and heritage advocacy groups are pushing for the revival of Escolta Street, which was once the premier street of the Philippines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Almost all of Manila's prewar and Spanish colonial architecture were destroyed during its <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1945)" title="Battle of Manila (1945)">battle for liberation</a> by the intensive bombardment of the United States Air Force during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Reconstruction took place afterwards, replacing the destroyed historic Spanish-era buildings with modern ones, erasing much of the city's character. Some buildings destroyed by the war have been reconstructed, such as the Old Legislative Building (now the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_(Manila)" title="National Museum of Fine Arts (Manila)">National Museum of Fine Arts</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ayuntamiento_de_Manila" title="Ayuntamiento de Manila">Ayuntamiento de Manila</a> (now the Bureau of the Treasury) and the currently under construction <a href="/wiki/San_Ignacio_Church_(Manila)" title="San Ignacio Church (Manila)">San Ignacio Church and Convent</a> (as the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_Intramuros" title="Museo de Intramuros">Museo de Intramuros</a>). There are plans to rehabilitate and/or restore several neglected historic buildings and places such as Plaza Del Carmen, <a href="/wiki/San_Sebastian_Church_(Manila)" title="San Sebastian Church (Manila)">San Sebastian Church</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Metropolitan_Theater" title="Manila Metropolitan Theater">Manila Metropolitan Theater</a>. Spanish-era shops and houses in the districts of <a href="/wiki/Binondo" title="Binondo">Binondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quiapo,_Manila" title="Quiapo, Manila">Quiapo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Nicolas,_Manila" title="San Nicolas, Manila">San Nicolas</a> are also planned to be restored, as a part of a movement to restore the city to its former glory and its beautiful prewar state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since Manila is prone to earthquakes, the Spanish colonial architects invented the style called Earthquake Baroque which the churches and government buildings during the Spanish colonial period adopted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-City_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-City-63">[63]</a></sup> As a result, succeeding earthquakes of the 18th and 19th centuries barely affected Manila, although it did periodically level the surrounding area. Modern buildings in and around Manila are designed or have been retrofitted to withstand an 8.2 magnitude quake in accordance to the country's building code.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Binondojf0070_25.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Binondojf0070_25.JPG/220px-Binondojf0070_25.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Binondojf0070_25.JPG/330px-Binondojf0070_25.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Binondojf0070_25.JPG/440px-Binondojf0070_25.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<p>According to the 2015 census, the population of the city was 1,780,148, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_Philippines" title="List of cities in the Philippines">second most populous city</a> in the Philippines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PSA15-NCR_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-PSA15-NCR-6">[6]</a></sup> Manila is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_proper_by_population_density" title="List of cities proper by population density">the most densely populated city</a> in the world, with 71,263 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup> in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PSApopden_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-PSApopden-7">[7]</a></sup> District 6 is listed as being the most dense with 68,266 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>, followed by District 1 with 64,936 and District 2 with 64,710, respectively. District 5 is the least densely populated area with 19,235.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manilapop_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-manilapop-90">[90]</a></sup> In the 2016 electoral roll, it had 974,479 registered voters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comelec_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-comelec-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manila's population density dwarfs that of <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a> (24,252 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> (20,482 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>), <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> (20,164 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>), <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">Dhaka</a> (29,069 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>), <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> (16,364 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>, with its most dense district, Nanshi, having a density of 56,785 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>), and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> (10,087 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manilapop_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-manilapop-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manila has been presumed to be the Philippines' largest city since the establishment of a permanent Spanish settlement with the city eventually becoming the political, commercial and ecclesiastical capital of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Its population increased dramatically since the 1903 census as the population tended to move from rural areas to towns and cities. In the 1960 census, Manila became the first Philippine city to breach the one million mark (more than 5 times of its 1903 population). The city continued to grow until the population somehow "stabilized" at 1.6 million and experienced alternating increase and decrease starting the 1990 census year. This phenomenon may be attributed to the higher growth experience by suburbs and the already very high population density of city. As such, Manila exhibited a decreasing percentage share to the metropolitan population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> from as high as 63% in the 1950s to 27.5%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> in 1980 and then to 13.8% in 2015. The much larger <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a> marginally surpassed the population of Manila in 1990 and by the 2015 census already has 1.1 million people more. Nationally, the population of Manila is expected to be overtaken by cities with larger territories such as <a href="/wiki/Caloocan" title="Caloocan">Caloocan City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Davao_City" title="Davao City">Davao City</a> by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The vernacular language is <a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">Filipino</a>, based mostly on the <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog language</a> of surrounding areas, and this Manila form of spoken Tagalog has essentially become the <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the Philippines, having spread throughout the archipelago through mass media and entertainment. <a href="/wiki/Philippine_English" title="Philippine English">English</a> is the language most widely used in education, business, and heavily in everyday usage throughout Metro Manila and the Philippines itself.</p>
<p>A number of older residents can still speak basic <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines" title="Spanish language in the Philippines">Spanish</a>, which used to be a mandatory subject in the curriculum of Philippine universities and colleges, and many children of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_settlement_in_the_Philippines" title="Japanese settlement in the Philippines">Japanese Filipino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koreans_in_the_Philippines" title="Koreans in the Philippines">Korean Filipino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Filipino" title="Indian Filipino">Indian Filipino</a>, and other migrants or expatriates also speak their parents' languages at home, aside from English and/or Filipino for everyday use. A variant of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Min" title="Southern Min">Southern Min</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lan-nang" title="Lan-nang">Hokkien</a> (locally known as <i>Lan'nang-oe</i>) is mainly spoken by the city's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese-Filipino" title="Chinese-Filipino">Chinese-Filipino</a> community.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Christianity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As a result of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Spain" title="Culture of Spain">Spanish</a> cultural influence, Manila is a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Philippines" title="Christianity in the Philippines">Christian</a> city. As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_the_Philippines" title="Catholic Church in the Philippines">Roman Catholics</a> were 83.5% of the population, followed by adherents of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Independent_Church" title="Philippine Independent Church">Philippine Independent Church</a> (2.4%); <a href="/wiki/Iglesia_ni_Cristo" title="Iglesia ni Cristo">Iglesia ni Cristo</a> (1.9%); various <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> churches (1.8%); and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a> (1.1%). Members of Islam and other religions make up the remaining 10.4% of the city's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manila is the site of prominent Catholic churches and institutions. There are 113 Catholic churches within the city limits; 63 are considered as major shrines, basilicas, or a cathedral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Manila_Cathedral" title="Manila Cathedral">Manila Cathedral</a> is the seat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Manila" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Manila">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Manila</a> and the oldest established church in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wow_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-wow-99">[99]</a></sup> Aside from the Manila Cathedral, there are also three other basilicas in the city: <a href="/wiki/Quiapo_Church" title="Quiapo Church">Quiapo Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Binondo_Church" title="Binondo Church">Binondo Church</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basilica_of_San_Sebastian,_Manila" title="Basilica of San Sebastian, Manila">Minor Basilica of San Sebastián</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Agustin_Church,_Manila" title="San Agustin Church, Manila">San Agustín Church</a> in Intramuros is a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> and is one of the two fully air-conditioned Catholic churches in the city. Manila also has other parishes located throughout the city, with some of them dating back to the Spanish Colonial Period when the city serves as the base for numerous Catholic missions both within the Philippines and to Asia beyond.</p>
<p>Several <a href="/wiki/Mainline_Protestant" title="Mainline Protestant">Mainline Protestant</a> denominations are headquartered in the city. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Parish_(Manila)" title="St. Stephen's Parish (Manila)">St. Stephen's Parish</a> <a href="/wiki/Pro-cathedral" title="Pro-cathedral">pro-cathedral</a> in the Sta. Cruz district is the see of the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_in_the_Philippines" title="Episcopal Church in the Philippines">Episcopal Church in the Philippines</a>' Diocese of Central Philippines, while align Taft Avenue are the main cathedral and central offices of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iglesia_Filipina_Independiente" title="Iglesia Filipina Independiente">Iglesia Filipina Independiente</a> (also called the Aglipayan Church, a <a href="/wiki/National_church" title="National church">national church</a> that was a product of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">Philippine Revolution</a>). Other faiths like <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">Mormons</a>) has several churches in the city.</p>
<p>The indigenous <a href="/wiki/Iglesia_ni_Cristo" title="Iglesia ni Cristo">Iglesia ni Cristo</a> has several locales (akin to parishes) in the city, including its very first chapel (now a museum) in Punta, Sta. Ana. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Christian" title="Evangelical Christian">Evangelical</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist" title="Seventh-day Adventist">Seventh-day Adventist</a> denominations also thrive within the city. The headquarters of the Philippine Bible Society is in Manila. Also, the main campus of the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Praise" title="Cathedral of Praise">Cathedral of Praise</a> is located along <a href="/wiki/Taft_Avenue" title="Taft Avenue">Taft Avenue</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesus_Is_Lord_Church" title="Jesus Is Lord Church">Jesus Is Lord Church</a> also has several branches and campuses in Manila, and celebrates its anniversary yearly at the Burnham Green and Quirino Grandstand in Rizal Park.</p>
