<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_faiths">Other faiths</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other faiths">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are many Buddhist and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoist" title="Taoist">Taoist</a> temples in the city serving the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Filipino" title="Chinese Filipino">Chinese Filipino</a> community. Quiapo is home to a sizable <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Philippines" title="Islam in the Philippines">Muslim</a> population which worships at <a href="/wiki/Masjid_Al-Dahab" title="Masjid Al-Dahab">Masjid Al-Dahab</a>. Members of the Indian expatriate population have the option of worshiping at the large <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_Philippines" title="Hinduism in the Philippines">Hindu</a> temple in the city, or at the <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikh</a> <a href="/wiki/Gurdwara" title="Gurdwara">gurdwara</a> along United Nations Avenue. The <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Assembly" title="Spiritual Assembly">National Spiritual Assembly</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahá'ís</a> of the Philippines, the governing body of the Filipino Bahá'í community, is headquartered near Manila's eastern border with Makati.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dtondo%3Dnorth_harbor%3Dinternational_container_terminal_-_view_from_world_trade_exchange_tower_binondo_-philippines--2015-0615--ls-.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dtondo%3Dnorth_harbor%3Dinternational_container_terminal_-_view_from_world_trade_exchange_tower_binondo_-philippines--2015-0615--ls-.JPG/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dtondo%3Dnorth_harbor%3Dinternational_container_terminal_-_view_from_world_trade_exchange_tower_binondo_-philippines--2015-0615--ls-.JPG/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dtondo%3Dnorth_harbor%3Dinternational_container_terminal_-_view_from_world_trade_exchange_tower_binondo_-philippines--2015-0615--ls-.JPG/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dbinondo%3Dchinatown_-_aerial_shot_from_riverview_mansion_-philippines--2015-0624--ls-.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dbinondo%3Dchinatown_-_aerial_shot_from_riverview_mansion_-philippines--2015-0624--ls-.JPG/220px-Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dbinondo%3Dchinatown_-_aerial_shot_from_riverview_mansion_-philippines--2015-0624--ls-.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dbinondo%3Dchinatown_-_aerial_shot_from_riverview_mansion_-philippines--2015-0624--ls-.JPG/330px-Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dbinondo%3Dchinatown_-_aerial_shot_from_riverview_mansion_-philippines--2015-0624--ls-.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dbinondo%3Dchinatown_-_aerial_shot_from_riverview_mansion_-philippines--2015-0624--ls-.JPG/440px-Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dbinondo%3Dchinatown_-_aerial_shot_from_riverview_mansion_-philippines--2015-0624--ls-.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dmm%3Dmanila%3Dbinondo%3Dchinatown_-_aerial_shot_from_riverview_mansion_-philippines--2015-0624--ls-.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of <a href="/wiki/Binondo" title="Binondo">Binondo</a>, the city's Chinatown and business district.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Manila is a major center for commerce, banking and finance, retailing, transportation, tourism, real estate, <a href="/wiki/New_media" title="New media">new media</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Old_media" title="Old media">traditional media</a>, advertising, legal services, accounting, insurance, theater, fashion, and the arts in the Philippines. Around 60,000 establishments operates in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The National Competitiveness Council of the Philippines which annually publishes the Cities and Municipalities Competitiveness Index (CMCI), ranks the cities, municipalities and provinces of the country according to their economic dynamism, government efficiency and infrastructure. According to the 2016 CMCI, Manila was the second most competitive city in the Philippines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Manila placed third in the Highly Urbanized City (HUC) category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Manila held the title country's most competitive city in 2015, and since then has been making it to the top 3, assuring that the city is consistently one of the best place to live in and do business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Lars Wittig, the country manager of Regus Philippines, hailed Manila as the third best city in the country to launch a start-up business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PIA-Start-up_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-PIA-Start-up-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Manila" title="Port of Manila">Port of Manila</a> is the largest seaport in the Philippines, making it the premier international shipping gateway to the country. The <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Ports_Authority" title="Philippine Ports Authority">Philippine Ports Authority</a> is the government agency responsible to oversee the operation and management of the ports. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Container_Terminal_Services_Inc." title="International Container Terminal Services Inc.">International Container Terminal Services Inc.</a> cited by the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> as one of the top five major maritime terminal operators in the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pse_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-pse-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-107">[107]</a></sup> has its headquarters and main operations on the ports of Manila. Another port operator, the Asian Terminal Incorporated, has its corporate office and main operations in the Manila South Harbor and its container depository located in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Mesa,_Manila" title="Santa Mesa, Manila">Santa Mesa</a>.</p>
<p>Binondo, the oldest and one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinatowns</a> in the world, was the center of commerce and business activities in the city. Numerous residential and office skyscrapers are found within its medieval streets. Plans to make the Chinatown area into a <a href="/wiki/Business_process_outsourcing" title="Business process outsourcing">business process outsourcing</a> (BPO) hub progresses and is aggressively pursued by the city government of Manila. 30 buildings are already identified to be converted into BPO offices. These buildings are mostly located along the Escolta Street of Binondo, which are all unoccupied and can be converted into offices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Divisoria in Tondo is known as the "shopping mecca of the Philippines". Numerous shopping malls are located in this place, which sells products and goods at bargain price. Small vendors occupy several roads that causes pedestrian and vehicular traffic. A famous landmark in Divisoria is the Tutuban Center, a large shopping mall that is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_National_Railways" title="Philippine National Railways">Philippine National Railways</a>' <a href="/wiki/Tutuban_railway_station" title="Tutuban railway station">Main Station</a>. It attracts 1 million people every month, but is expected to add another 400,000 people when the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Light_Rail_Transit_System_Line_2" title="Manila Light Rail Transit System Line 2">LRT Line 2</a> West Extension is constructed, which is set to make it as Manila's busiest transfer station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CCPjf0186_04.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/CCPjf0186_04.JPG/220px-CCPjf0186_04.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/CCPjf0186_04.JPG/330px-CCPjf0186_04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/CCPjf0186_04.JPG/440px-CCPjf0186_04.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CCPjf0186_04.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bangko_Sentral_ng_Pilipinas" title="Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas">Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas</a>, the central bank of the Philippines</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Diverse manufacturers within the city produce industrial-related products such as chemicals, textiles, clothing, and electronic goods. Food and beverages and tobacco products also produced. Local entrepreneurs continue to process primary commodities for export, including rope, plywood, refined sugar, <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a>, and coconut oil. The food-processing industry is one of the most stable major manufacturing sector in the city.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pandacan_oil_depot" title="Pandacan oil depot">Pandacan Oil Depot</a> houses the storage facilities and distribution terminals of the three major players in the country's petroleum industry, namely <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Caltex Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Pilipinas Shell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petron_Corporation" title="Petron Corporation">Petron Corporation</a>. The oil depot has been a subject of various concerns, including its environmental and health impact to the residents of Manila. The Supreme Court has ordered that the oil depot to be relocated outside the city by July 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> but it failed to meet this deadline. Most of the oil depot facility inside the 33 hectare compound have been demolished, and plans are put into place to transform it into a transport hub or even a food park.</p>
<p>Manila is a major publishing center in the Philippines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-112">[112]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Manila_Bulletin" title="Manila Bulletin">Manila Bulletin</a></i>, the Philippines' largest broadsheet newspaper by circulation, is headquartered in Intramuros.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manila_Bulletin_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manila_Bulletin-113">[113]</a></sup> Other major publishing companies in the country like <i><a href="/wiki/The_Manila_Times" title="The Manila Times">The Manila Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Philippine_Star" title="The Philippine Star">The Philippine Star</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila_Standard_Today" title="Manila Standard Today">Manila Standard Today</a></i> are headquartered in the Port Area. The <i><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Commercial_News" title="Chinese Commercial News">Chinese Commercial News</a></i>, the Philippines' oldest existing Chinese-language newspaper, and the country's third-oldest existing newspaper<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memorial_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-memorial-114">[114]</a></sup> is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Binondo" title="Binondo">Binondo</a>.</p>
<p>Manila serves as the headquarters of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_Philippines" title="Central Bank of the Philippines">Central Bank of the Philippines</a> which is located along <a href="/wiki/Roxas_Boulevard" title="Roxas Boulevard">Roxas Boulevard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BSP_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-BSP-115">[115]</a></sup> Some universal banks in the Philippines that has its headquarters in the city are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landbank_of_the_Philippines" title="Landbank of the Philippines">Landbank of the Philippines</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Trust_Company" title="Philippine Trust Company">Philippine Trust Company</a>. <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever Philippines</a> has its corporate office along <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Avenue" title="United Nations Avenue">United Nations Avenue</a> in <a href="/wiki/Paco,_Manila" title="Paco, Manila">Paco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Unilever_Phils_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Unilever_Phils-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, a company listed in the <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Global_2000" title="Forbes Global 2000">Forbes Global 2000</a>, also has its regional office along UN Avenue.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Manila" title="Tourism in Manila">Tourism in Manila</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Intramuros_Manila.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Intramuros_Manila.jpg/220px-Intramuros_Manila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Intramuros_Manila.jpg/330px-Intramuros_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Intramuros_Manila.jpg/440px-Intramuros_Manila.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Intramuros_Manila.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The historic <a href="/wiki/Fort_Santiago" title="Fort Santiago">Fort Santiago</a> in <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Manila welcomes over 1 million tourists each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-112">[112]</a></sup> Major tourist destinations include the historic Walled City of <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Center_of_the_Philippines_Complex" title="Cultural Center of the Philippines Complex">Cultural Center of the Philippines Complex</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manila_Note_II_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manila_Note_II-117">[note 1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Manila_Ocean_Park" title="Manila Ocean Park">Manila Ocean Park</a>, Binondo (Chinatown), Ermita, <a href="/wiki/Malate,_Manila" title="Malate, Manila">Malate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manila_Zoo" title="Manila Zoo">Manila Zoo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_Philippines" title="National Museum of the Philippines">National Museum Complex</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Park" title="Rizal Park">Rizal Park</a>. Both the historic Walled City of Intramuros and Rizal Park were designated as flagship destinations and as a tourism enterprise zones in the Tourism Act of 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TourismAct_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-TourismAct-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rizal Park, also known as Luneta Park, is the national park and the largest urban park in Asia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> with an area of 58 hectares (140 acres),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> The park was constructed as an honor and dedication to the country's national hero <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal" title="José Rizal">José Rizal</a>, who was executed by the Spaniards on charges of subversion. The flagpole west of the Rizal Monument is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilometre_Zero" title="Kilometre Zero">Kilometer Zero</a> marker for distances to the rest of the country. The park was managed by the National Parks and Development Committee.</p>
<p>The 0.67 square kilometers (0.26 sq mi) Walled City of <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a> is the historic center of Manila. It is administered by the Intramuros Administration, an attached agency of the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Tourism_(Philippines)" title="Department of Tourism (Philippines)">Department of Tourism</a>. It contains the famed <a href="/wiki/Manila_Cathedral" title="Manila Cathedral">Manila Cathedral</a> and the 18th Century <a href="/wiki/San_Agustin_Church_(Manila)" title="San Agustin Church (Manila)">San Agustin Church</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kalesa" title="Kalesa">Kalesa</a> is a popular mode of transportation for tourists in Intramuros and nearby places including Binondo, Ermita and Rizal Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Known as the oldest <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">chinatown</a> in the world, <a href="/wiki/Binondo" title="Binondo">Binondo</a> was established on 1521 and it was already a hub of Chinese commerce even before the Spaniards colonized the Philippines. Its main attractions are <a href="/wiki/Binondo_Church" title="Binondo Church">Binondo Church</a>, Filipino-Chinese Friendship Arch, Seng Guan Buddhist temple and authentic Chinese restaurants.</p>
<p>Manila is designated as the country's pioneer of <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a>, expecting it to generate $1 billion in revenue annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> However, lack of progressive health system, inadequate infrastructure and the unstable political environment are seen as hindrances for its growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rob_wiki.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Rob_wiki.JPG/220px-Rob_wiki.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Rob_wiki.JPG/330px-Rob_wiki.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Rob_wiki.JPG/440px-Rob_wiki.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rob_wiki.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Robinsons_Place_Manila" title="Robinsons Place Manila">Robinsons Place Manila</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ermita" title="Ermita">Ermita</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Manila is regarded as one of the best shopping destinations in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> Major <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping malls</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_stores" title="Department stores">department stores</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Market_(place)" title="Market (place)">markets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supermarket" title="Supermarket">supermarkets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaars</a> thrives within the city.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Robinsons_Place_Manila" title="Robinsons Place Manila">Robinsons Place Manila</a> is the largest shopping mall in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> The mall was the second and the largest <a href="/wiki/Robinsons_Malls" title="Robinsons Malls">Robinsons Malls</a> built. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SM_Supermall" title="SM Supermall">SM Supermall</a> operates two shopping malls in the city which are the SM City Manila and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SM_City_San_Lazaro" title="SM City San Lazaro">SM City San Lazaro</a>. SM City Manila is located on the former grounds of YMCA Manila beside the <a href="/wiki/Manila_City_Hall" title="Manila City Hall">Manila City Hall</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ermita,_Manila" title="Ermita, Manila">Ermita</a>, while SM City San Lazaro is built on the site of the former San Lazaro Hippodrome in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Manila" title="Santa Cruz, Manila">Sta. Cruz</a>. The building of the former Manila Royal Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Quiapo,_Manila" title="Quiapo, Manila">Quiapo</a>, which is famed for its revolving restaurant atop, is now the <a href="/wiki/SM_Quiapo" title="SM Quiapo">SM Clearance Center</a> that was established in 1972.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> The site of the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SM_Department_Store" title="SM Department Store">SM Store</a> is located at Carlos Palanca Sr. (formerly Echague) Street in <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_Manila" title="San Miguel, Manila">San Miguel</a>.</p>
<p>One of Recto Avenue's famous destinations is <a href="/wiki/Divisoria" title="Divisoria">Divisoria</a>, home to numerous shopping malls in the city, including the famed Tutuban Center and the <a href="/wiki/Lucky_Chinatown" title="Lucky Chinatown">Lucky Chinatown Mall</a>. It is also dubbed as the shopping mecca of the Philippines where everything is sold at bargain price. Binondo, the oldest Chinatown in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-en.radio86.com_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-en.radio86.com-27">[27]</a></sup> is the city's center of commerce and trade for all types of businesses run by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino-Chinese" title="Filipino-Chinese">Filipino-Chinese</a> merchants with a wide variety of Chinese and Filipino shops and restaurants. Quiapo is referred to as the "Old Downtown", where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiangge" title="Tiangge">tiangges</a>, markets, boutique shops, music and electronics stores are common. <a href="/wiki/Recto_Avenue" title="Recto Avenue">C.M. Recto Avenue</a> is where lots of department stores are located.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:04762jfNational_Museum_of_the_Philippines_Ermita_Manilafvf_07.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/04762jfNational_Museum_of_the_Philippines_Ermita_Manilafvf_07.jpg/220px-04762jfNational_Museum_of_the_Philippines_Ermita_Manilafvf_07.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/04762jfNational_Museum_of_the_Philippines_Ermita_Manilafvf_07.jpg/330px-04762jfNational_Museum_of_the_Philippines_Ermita_Manilafvf_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/04762jfNational_Museum_of_the_Philippines_Ermita_Manilafvf_07.jpg/440px-04762jfNational_Museum_of_the_Philippines_Ermita_Manilafvf_07.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:04762jfNational_Museum_of_the_Philippines_Ermita_Manilafvf_07.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_(Manila)" title="National Museum of Fine Arts (Manila)">National Museum of Fine Arts</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the cultural center of the Philippines, Manila is the home to a number of museums. The National Museum Complex of the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_Philippines" title="National Museum of the Philippines">National Museum of the Philippines</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Park" title="Rizal Park">Rizal Park</a>, is composed of the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_(Manila)" title="National Museum of Fine Arts (Manila)">National Museum of Fine Arts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Anthropology_(Manila)" title="National Museum of Anthropology (Manila)">National Museum of Anthropology</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Natural_History_(Manila)" title="National Museum of Natural History (Manila)">National Museum of Natural History</a>. The famous painting <a href="/wiki/Juan_Luna" title="Juan Luna">Juan Luna</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Spoliarium" title="Spoliarium">Spoliarium</a>, can be found in the complex. The city also hosts the repository of the country's printed and recorded cultural heritage and other literary and information resources, the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_the_Philippines" title="National Library of the Philippines">National Library</a>. Museums established or run by educational institutions are the <a href="/wiki/Mabini_Shrine_(Manila)" title="Mabini Shrine (Manila)">Mabini Shrine</a>, the DLS-CSB Museum of Contemporary Art and Design, <a href="/wiki/UST_Museum_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="UST Museum of Arts and Sciences">UST Museum of Arts and Sciences</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines_Museum_of_a_History_of_Ideas" title="University of the Philippines Museum of a History of Ideas">UP Museum of a History of Ideas</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Museum_of_Natural_History_(Manila)_Facade_-_Front_View.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="4096" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/National_Museum_of_Natural_History_%28Manila%29_Facade_-_Front_View.jpg/220px-National_Museum_of_Natural_History_%28Manila%29_Facade_-_Front_View.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/National_Museum_of_Natural_History_%28Manila%29_Facade_-_Front_View.jpg/330px-National_Museum_of_Natural_History_%28Manila%29_Facade_-_Front_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/National_Museum_of_Natural_History_%28Manila%29_Facade_-_Front_View.jpg/440px-National_Museum_of_Natural_History_%28Manila%29_Facade_-_Front_View.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Museum_of_Natural_History_(Manila)_Facade_-_Front_View.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Natural_History_(Manila)" title="National Museum of Natural History (Manila)">National Museum of Natural History</a> at Agrifina Circle, <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Park" title="Rizal Park">Rizal Park</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bahay_Tsinoy" title="Bahay Tsinoy">Bahay Tsinoy</a>, one of Manila's most prominent museums, documents the Chinese lives and contributions in the history of the Philippines. The Intramuros Light and Sound Museum chronicles the Filipinos desire for freedom during <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">the revolution</a> under Rizal's leadership and other revolutionary leaders. The <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Manila" title="Metropolitan Museum of Manila">Metropolitan Museum of Manila</a> is a museum of modern and contemporary visual arts exhibits the Filipino arts and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Philippines" title="Culture of the Philippines">culture</a>.</p>
<p>Other museums in the city are the Museum of Manila, the city-owned museum that exhibits the city's culture and history, <a href="/wiki/Museo_Pambata" title="Museo Pambata">Museo Pambata</a>, a children's museum and a place of hands-on discovery and fun learning, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Philippine_Political_History" title="Museum of Philippine Political History">Museum of Philippine Political History</a>, which exhibits notable political events in the country, and Plaza San Luis, an outdoor heritage public museum that contains a collection of nine Spanish Bahay na Bató houses. Ecclesiastical museums in the located in the city are the Parish of the Our Lady of the Abandoned in Santa Ana, the <a href="/wiki/San_Agustin_Church_(Manila)" title="San Agustin Church (Manila)">San Agustin Church Museum</a> and the upcoming <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_Intramuros" title="Museo de Intramuros">Museo de Intramuros</a> which was housed in the reconstructed <a href="/wiki/San_Ignacio_Church_(Manila)" title="San Ignacio Church (Manila)">San Ignacio Church and Convent</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1073" data-file-width="1600" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg/220px-Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg/330px-Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg/440px-Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Children playing basketball at the ruins of <a href="/wiki/San_Ignacio_Church_(Manila)" title="San Ignacio Church (Manila)">San Ignacio Church</a> in <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Intramurosjf0400_16.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Intramurosjf0400_16.JPG/220px-Intramurosjf0400_16.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Intramurosjf0400_16.JPG/330px-Intramurosjf0400_16.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Intramurosjf0400_16.JPG/440px-Intramurosjf0400_16.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Intramurosjf0400_16.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Intramuros Golf Club</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sports in Manila have a long and distinguished history. The city's, and in general the country's main sport is <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, and most barangays have a basketball court or at least a makeshift basketball court, with court markings drawn on the streets. Larger barangays have covered courts where inter-barangay leagues are held every summer (April to May). Manila has many sports venues, such as the <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Sports_Complex" title="Rizal Memorial Sports Complex">Rizal Memorial Sports Complex</a> and San Andres Gym, the home of the now defunct <a href="/wiki/Manila_Metrostars" title="Manila Metrostars">Manila Metrostars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> The Rizal Memorial Sports Complex houses the Rizal Memorial Track and Football Stadium, the Baseball Stadium, Tennis Courts, Memorial Coliseum and the Ninoy Aquino Stadium (the latter two are indoor arenas). The Rizal complex had hosted several multi-sport events, such as the <a href="/wiki/1954_Asian_Games" title="1954 Asian Games">1954 Asian Games</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1934_Far_Eastern_Games" title="1934 Far Eastern Games">1934 Far Eastern Games</a>. Whenever the country hosts the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_Games" title="Southeast Asian Games">Southeast Asian Games</a>, most of the events are held at the complex, but in the <a href="/wiki/2005_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="2005 Southeast Asian Games">2005 Games</a>, most events were held elsewhere. The <a href="/wiki/1960_ABC_Championship" title="1960 ABC Championship">1960 ABC Championship</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1973_ABC_Championship" title="1973 ABC Championship">1973 ABC Championship</a>, forerunners of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIBA_Asia_Championship" title="FIBA Asia Championship">FIBA Asia Championship</a>, was hosted by the complex, with the <a href="/wiki/Philippines_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Philippines men's national basketball team">national basketball team</a> winning on both tournaments. The <a href="/wiki/1978_FIBA_World_Championship" title="1978 FIBA World Championship">1978 FIBA World Championship</a> was held at the complex although the latter stages were held in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Araneta_Coliseum" title="Araneta Coliseum">Araneta Coliseum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a>, Southeast Asia's largest indoor arena at that time.</p>
<p>Manila also hosts several well-known sports facilities such as the <a href="/wiki/Enrique_M._Razon_Sports_Center" title="Enrique M. Razon Sports Center">Enrique M. Razon Sports Center</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas_Sports_Complex" title="University of Santo Tomas Sports Complex">University of Santo Tomas Sports Complex</a>, both of which are private venues owned by a university; collegiate sports are also held, with the <a href="/wiki/University_Athletic_Association_of_the_Philippines" title="University Athletic Association of the Philippines">University Athletic Association of the Philippines</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association_(Philippines)" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association (Philippines)">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> basketball games held at Rizal Memorial Coliseum and Ninoy Aquino Stadium, although basketball events had transferred to <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Metro_Manila" title="San Juan, Metro Manila">San Juan</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filoil_Flying_V_Arena" title="Filoil Flying V Arena">Filoil Flying V Arena</a> and the Araneta Coliseum in Quezon City. Other collegiate sports are still held at the Rizal Memorial Sports Complex. Professional basketball also used to play at the city, but the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Basketball_Association" title="Philippine Basketball Association">Philippine Basketball Association</a> now holds their games at Araneta Coliseum and <a href="/wiki/Cuneta_Astrodome" title="Cuneta Astrodome">Cuneta Astrodome</a> at <a href="/wiki/Pasay" title="Pasay">Pasay</a>; the now defunct <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Basketball_League" title="Philippine Basketball League">Philippine Basketball League</a> played some of their games at the Rizal Memorial Sports Complex.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Manila_Storm" title="Manila Storm">Manila Storm</a> are the city's <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> team training at Rizal Park (Luneta Park) and playing their matches at Southern Plains Field, <a href="/wiki/Calamba,_Laguna" title="Calamba, Laguna">Calamba, Laguna</a>. Previously a widely played sport in the city, Manila is now the home of the only sizable <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> stadium in the country, at the <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Baseball_Stadium" title="Rizal Memorial Baseball Stadium">Rizal Memorial Baseball Stadium</a>. The stadium hosts games of <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Philippines" title="Baseball Philippines">Baseball Philippines</a>; <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a> and <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> were the first players to score a <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home run</a> at the stadium at their tour of the country on December 2, 1934.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> Another popular sport in the city are <a href="/wiki/Cue_sports" title="Cue sports">cue sports</a>, and billiard halls are a feature in most barangays. The <a href="/wiki/2010_World_Cup_of_Pool" title="2010 World Cup of Pool">2010 World Cup of Pool</a> was held at <a href="/wiki/Robinsons_Place_Manila" title="Robinsons Place Manila">Robinsons Place Manila</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Stadium" title="Rizal Memorial Stadium">Rizal Memorial Track and Football Stadium</a> hosted the first <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> qualifier in decades when the <a href="/wiki/Philippines_national_football_team" title="Philippines national football team">Philippines</a> hosted <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_basketball_team" title="Sri Lanka national basketball team">Sri Lanka</a> in July 2011. The stadium, which was previously unfit for international matches, had undergone a major renovation program before the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> The Football Stadium now regularly hosts matches of the <a href="/wiki/United_Football_League_(Philippines)" title="United Football League (Philippines)">United Football League</a>. The stadium also hosted its first <a href="/wiki/Test_match_(rugby_union)" title="Test match (rugby union)">rugby test</a> when it hosted the <a href="/wiki/2012_Asian_Five_Nations_division_tournaments" title="2012 Asian Five Nations division tournaments">2012 Asian Five Nations Division I</a> tournaments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivities_and_holidays">Festivities and holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Festivities and holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_Philippines" title="Public holidays in the Philippines">Public holidays in the Philippines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_Nazarene_procession.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Black_Nazarene_procession.jpg/220px-Black_Nazarene_procession.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Black_Nazarene_procession.jpg/330px-Black_Nazarene_procession.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Black_Nazarene_procession.jpg/440px-Black_Nazarene_procession.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Black_Nazarene_procession.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Catholic devotees during the <a href="/wiki/Black_Nazarene" title="Black Nazarene">Feast of the Black Nazarene</a> (<i>Traslacíon</i>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Manila celebrates civic and national holidays. Since most of the city's citizens are <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> most of the festivities are religious in nature. Manila Day, which celebrates the city's founding on June 24, 1571 by <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel López de Legazpi">Miguel López de Legazpi</a>, was first proclaimed by <a href="/wiki/Herminio_A._Astorga" title="Herminio A. Astorga">Herminio A. Astorga</a> (then Vice Mayor of Manila) on June 24, 1962. It has been annually commemorated under the <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patronage</a> of <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John the Baptist</a>, and has always been declared by the national government as a special non-working holiday through Presidential Proclamations. Each of the city's 897 barangays also have their own festivities guided by their own <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a>.</p>
<p>The city is also the host to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Nazarene" title="Black Nazarene">Feast of the Black Nazarene</a>, held every January 9, which draws millions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Catholic</a> devotees. Other religious festivities held in Manila are the Feast of Santo Niño in Tondo and Pandacan held on the third Sunday of January and the Feast of the Nuestra Señora de los Desamparados de Manila (Our Lady of the Abandoned), the patron saint of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana,_Manila" title="Santa Ana, Manila">Santa Ana</a> and held every May 12. Non-religious holidays include the <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Heroes%27_Day" title="National Heroes' Day">National Heroes' Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonifacio_Day" title="Bonifacio Day">Bonifacio Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rizal_Day" title="Rizal Day">Rizal Day</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Law and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Intramurosjf0305_17.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Intramurosjf0305_17.JPG/220px-Intramurosjf0305_17.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Intramurosjf0305_17.JPG/330px-Intramurosjf0305_17.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Intramurosjf0305_17.JPG/440px-Intramurosjf0305_17.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Intramurosjf0305_17.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Manila_City_Hall" title="Manila City Hall">Manila City Hall</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_(Cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="928" data-file-width="1650" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28Cropped%29.jpg/220px-Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28Cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28Cropped%29.jpg/330px-Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28Cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28Cropped%29.jpg/440px-Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28Cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_(Cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace" title="Malacañang Palace">Malacañang Palace</a> is the official residence and office of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Philippines" title="President of the Philippines">President of the Philippines</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Del_Gobernador.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Palacio_Del_Gobernador.JPG/220px-Palacio_Del_Gobernador.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Palacio_Del_Gobernador.JPG/330px-Palacio_Del_Gobernador.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Palacio_Del_Gobernador.JPG/440px-Palacio_Del_Gobernador.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Del_Gobernador.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Palacio_del_Gobernador" title="Palacio del Gobernador">Palacio del Gobernador</a> in <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a> is home to the Philippine <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Elections_(Philippines)" title="Commission on Elections (Philippines)">Commission on Elections</a> and Intramuros Administration.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Supreme_Court_in_Manila.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Supreme_Court_in_Manila.JPG/220px-Supreme_Court_in_Manila.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Supreme_Court_in_Manila.JPG/330px-Supreme_Court_in_Manila.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Supreme_Court_in_Manila.JPG/440px-Supreme_Court_in_Manila.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Supreme_Court_in_Manila.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines" title="Supreme Court of the Philippines">Supreme Court of the Philippines</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Manila—officially known as the City of Manila—is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">national capital</a> of the Philippines and is classified as a Special City (according to its income)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Cities_of_the_Philippines#classification" title="Cities of the Philippines">Highly Urbanized City</a> (HUC). The <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Manila" title="Mayor of Manila">mayor</a> is the chief executive, and is assisted by the vice mayor, the 36-member City Council, six Congressmen, the President of the Association of Barangay Captains, and the President of the <i><a href="/wiki/Sangguniang_Kabataan" title="Sangguniang Kabataan">Sangguniang Kabataan</a></i>. The members of the City Council are elected as representatives of specific congressional districts within the city. The city, however, have no control over Intramuros and the Manila North Harbor. The historic Walled City is administered by the Intramuros Administration, while the Manila North Harbor is managed by the Philippine Ports Authority. Both are national government agencies. The barangays that have jurisdictions over these places only oversee the welfare of the city's constituents and cannot exercise their executive powers.</p>
<p>The current <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Manila" title="Mayor of Manila">mayor</a> is <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Estrada" title="Joseph Estrada">Joseph Estrada</a>, who served as the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Philippines" title="President of the Philippines">President of the Philippines</a> from 1998 to 2001. He is currently on his second term in serving as the city mayor. The current vice mayor is Dr. Maria Shielah "Honey" Lacuna-Pangan, daughter of former Manila Vice Mayor Danny Lacuna. The mayor and the vice mayor are term-limited by up to 3 terms, with each term lasting for 3 years.</p>
<p>Manila, being the seat of political power of the Philippines, has several national government offices headquartered at the city. Planning for the development for being the center of government started during the early years of <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)" title="History of the Philippines (1898–1946)">American colonization</a> when they envisioned a well-designed city outside the walls of Intramuros. The strategic location chosen was Bagumbayan, a former town which is now the Rizal Park to become the center of government and a design commission was given to <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Burnham" title="Daniel Burnham">Daniel Burnham</a> to create a master plan for the city patterned after <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> These improvements were eventually abandoned under the Commonwealth Government of <a href="/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon" title="Manuel L. Quezon">Manuel L. Quezon</a>.</p>
<p>A new government center was to be built on the hills northeast of Manila, or what is now Quezon City. Several government agencies have set up their headquarters in Quezon City but several key government offices still reside in Manila. However, many of the plans were substantially altered after the devastation of Manila during World War II and by subsequent administrations.</p>
<p>The city, as the capital, still hosts the Office of the President, as well as the president's official residence. Aside from these, important government agencies and institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines" title="Supreme Court of the Philippines">Supreme Court</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Court_of_Appeals" title="Philippine Court of Appeals">Court of Appeals</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bangko_Sentral_ng_Pilipinas" title="Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas">Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_Departments_of_the_Philippines" title="Executive Departments of the Philippines">Departments</a> of <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Budget_and_Management_(Philippines)" title="Department of Budget and Management (Philippines)">Budget and Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Finance_(Philippines)" title="Department of Finance (Philippines)">Finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health_(Philippines)" title="Department of Health (Philippines)">Health</a>, <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Justice_(Philippines)" title="Department of Justice (Philippines)">Justice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Labor_and_Employment_(Philippines)" title="Department of Labor and Employment (Philippines)">Labor and Employment</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_Public_Works_and_Highways" title="Department of Public Works and Highways">Public Works and Highways</a> still call the city home. Manila also hosts important national institutions such as the National Library, National Archives, National Museum and the Philippine General Hospital.</p>
<p>Congress previously held office at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Legislative_Building_(Manila)" title="Old Legislative Building (Manila)">Old Congress Building</a>. In 1972, due to declaration of martial law, Congress was dissolved; its successor, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Batasang_Pambansa" title="Batasang Pambansa">Batasang Pambansa</a>, held office at the new <a href="/wiki/Batasang_Pambansa_Complex" title="Batasang Pambansa Complex">Batasang Pambansa Complex</a>. When a new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Philippines" title="Constitution of the Philippines">constitution</a> restored the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> Congress, the House of Representatives stayed at the Batasang Pambansa Complex, while the Senate remained at the Old Congress Building. In May 1997, the Senate transferred to a new building it shares with the <a href="/wiki/Government_Service_Insurance_System" title="Government Service Insurance System">Government Service Insurance System</a> at reclaimed land at <a href="/wiki/Pasay" title="Pasay">Pasay</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines" title="Supreme Court of the Philippines">Supreme Court</a> will also transfer to its new campus at <a href="/wiki/Bonifacio_Global_City" title="Bonifacio Global City">Bonifacio Global City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taguig" title="Taguig">Taguig</a> in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2016 Annual Financial Report for Local Government published by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commission_on_Audit_(Philippines)" title="Commission on Audit (Philippines)">Commission on Audit</a>, it is stated that the City of Manila's total income was ₱12.8 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016audit_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-2016audit-137">[136]</a></sup> It is one of the cities with the highest tax collection and internal revenue allotment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> Tax collection alone accounts for ₱8.6 billion out of the total ₱12.8 billion city income in 2016, while the city's total Internal Revenue Allotment from the National Treasury amounts to ₱2.086 billion. Its total asset was worth ₱36.1 billion in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016audit_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-2016audit-137">[136]</a></sup> The City of Manila has the highest budget allocation to healthcare among all the cities and municipalities in the Philippines. Manila has a total of 14,586 personnel complement by the end of 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COA2015_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-COA2015-139">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Barangays_and_Districts">Barangays and Districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Barangays and Districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Unofficial_Manila_Map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6300" data-file-width="4500" height="350" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Unofficial_Manila_Map.jpg/250px-Unofficial_Manila_Map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Unofficial_Manila_Map.jpg/375px-Unofficial_Manila_Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Unofficial_Manila_Map.jpg/500px-Unofficial_Manila_Map.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

District Map of Manila that shows its 16 districts.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><br/>
Manila is made up of 897 <a href="/wiki/Barangay" title="Barangay">barangays</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MNLLN_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-MNLLN-140">[139]</a></sup> which are grouped into 100 Zones for statistical convenience. Manila has the most number of barangays in the Philippines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> Attempts at reducing its number have not prospered despite local legislation—Ordinance 7907, passed on 23 April 1996—reducing the number from 897 to 150 by merging existing barangays, because of the failure to hold a plebiscite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Manila#1st_District" title="Legislative districts of Manila">District I</a></b> (2015 population: 415,906)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LDpop_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-LDpop-143">[142]</a></sup> covers the western part of Tondo and is the most densely populated Congressional District. It is the home to one of the biggest urban poor communities. The <a href="/wiki/Smokey_Mountain" title="Smokey Mountain">Smokey Mountain</a> in Balut Island is once known as the largest landfill where thousands of impoverished people lives in the slums. After the closure of the landfill in 1995, mid-rise housing buildings were built in place. This district also contains the Manila North Harbour Centre, the Manila North Harbor, and the Manila International Container Terminal of the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Manila" title="Port of Manila">Port of Manila</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Manila#2nd_District" title="Legislative districts of Manila">District II</a></b> (2015 population: 215,457)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LDpop_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-LDpop-143">[142]</a></sup> covers the eastern part of Tondo known as Gagalangin. It contains Divisoria, a popular shopping place in the Philippines and the site of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tutuban_(PNR_station)" title="Tutuban (PNR station)">Main Terminal Station</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_National_Railways" title="Philippine National Railways">Philippine National Railways</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Manila#3rd_District" title="Legislative districts of Manila">District III</a></b> (2015 population: 221,780)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LDpop_143-2"><a href="#cite_note-LDpop-143">[142]</a></sup> covers Binondo, Quiapo, San Nicolas and Santa Cruz. It encompasses the so-called "Downtown Manila" or traditional business district of the city and the oldest Chinatown in the world.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Manila#4th_District" title="Legislative districts of Manila">District IV</a></b> (2015 population: 265,046)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LDpop_143-3"><a href="#cite_note-LDpop-143">[142]</a></sup> covers Sampaloc and some parts of Santa Mesa. It contains the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas" title="University of Santo Tomas">University of Santo Tomas</a>, the oldest existing university in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Manila#5th_District" title="Legislative districts of Manila">District V</a></b> (2015 population: 366,714)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LDpop_143-4"><a href="#cite_note-LDpop-143">[142]</a></sup> covers Ermita, Malate, Paco, Port Area, Intramuros, San Andres Bukid, and a portion of Santa Ana. The historic Walled City is located here, along with <a href="/wiki/Manila_Cathedral" title="Manila Cathedral">Manila Cathedral</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Agustin_Church_(Manila)" title="San Agustin Church (Manila)">San Agustin Church</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Manila#6th_District" title="Legislative districts of Manila">District VI</a></b> (2007 population: 295,245)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LDpop_143-5"><a href="#cite_note-LDpop-143">[142]</a></sup> covers Pandacan, San Miguel, Santa Ana, Santa Mesa and a portion of Paco. Santa Ana district is known for its 18th Century <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Church" title="Santa Ana Church">Santa Ana Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Historic_houses_in_Santa_Ana,_Manila" title="Historic houses in Santa Ana, Manila">historic ancestral houses</a>. <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_University_of_the_Philippines" title="Polytechnic University of the Philippines">Polytechnic University of the Philippines</a> is located here, the most populous university in the Philippines.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Metro_Manila" title="Transportation in Metro Manila">Transportation in Metro Manila</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_transport_in_Manila" title="Public transport in Manila">Public transport in Manila</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_roads_in_Metro_Manila" title="Major roads in Metro Manila">Major roads in Metro Manila</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1424" data-file-width="2144" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG/220px-WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG/330px-WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG/440px-WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg/220px-LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg/330px-LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg/440px-LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
