<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blumentritt_LRT_Station" title="Blumentritt LRT Station">Blumentritt Station</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Light_Rail_Transit_System_Line_1" title="Manila Light Rail Transit System Line 1">LRT-1</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>One of the more famous modes of transportation in Manila is the <a href="/wiki/Jeepney" title="Jeepney">jeepney</a>. Patterned after <a href="/wiki/Jeep#World_War_II_Jeeps" title="Jeep">U.S. Army jeeps</a>, these have been in use since the years immediately following World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> The Tamaraw FX, the third generation <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Kijang" title="Toyota Kijang">Toyota Kijang</a>, which competed directly with jeepneys and followed fixed routes for a set price, once plied the streets of Manila. All types of public road transport plying Manila are privately owned and operated under government franchise.</p>
<p>On a for-hire basis, the city is served by numerous <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">taxicabs</a>, "tricycles" (motorcycles with sidecars, the Philippine version of the <a href="/wiki/Auto_rickshaw" title="Auto rickshaw">auto rickshaw</a>), and "<i>trisikads</i>" or "<i>sikads</i>", which are also known as "<i>kuligligs</i>" (bicycles with a sidecars, the Philippine version of <a href="/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw" title="Cycle rickshaw">pedicabs</a>). In some areas, especially in Divisoria, motorized pedicabs are popular. Spanish-era horse-drawn <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calesa" title="Calesa">calesas</a> are still a popular tourist attraction and mode of transportation in the streets of Binondo and Intramuros. By October 2016, the city will phase out all gasoline-run tricycles and pedicabs and replace them with electric tricycles (e-trikes). The city plans to distribute 10,000 e-trikes to qualified tricycle drivers from the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is serviced by the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Light_Rail_Transit_System_Line_1" title="Manila Light Rail Transit System Line 1">LRT Line 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manila_Light_Rail_Transit_System_Line_2" title="Manila Light Rail Transit System Line 2">Line 2</a>, which form the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Light_Rail_Transit_System" title="Manila Light Rail Transit System">Manila Light Rail Transit System</a>. Development of the railway system began in the 1970s under the presidency of Ferdinand Marcos, when Line 1 was built, making it the first light rail transport in Southeast Asia. These systems are currently undergoing a multibillion-dollar expansion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10points_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-10points-147">[146]</a></sup> Line 1 runs along the length of <a href="/wiki/Taft_Avenue" title="Taft Avenue">Taft Avenue</a> (N170/R-2) and Rizal Avenue (N150/R-9), and Line 2 runs along Claro M. Recto Avenue (N145/C-1) and Ramon Magsaysay Boulevard (N180/R-6) from <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Manila" title="Santa Cruz, Manila">Santa Cruz</a>, through <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a>, up to Masinag in <a href="/wiki/Antipolo" title="Antipolo">Antipolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rizal" title="Rizal">Rizal</a>.</p>
<p>The main terminal of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_National_Railways" title="Philippine National Railways">Philippine National Railways</a> lies within the city. One commuter railway within Metro Manila is in operation. The line runs in a general north-south direction from Tutuban (Tondo) toward Laguna. The Port of Manila, located in the vicinity of Manila Bay, is the chief seaport of the Philippines. The <a href="/wiki/Pasig_River_Ferry_Service" title="Pasig River Ferry Service">Pasig River Ferry Service</a> which runs on the Pasig River is another form of transportation. The city is also served by the <a href="/wiki/Ninoy_Aquino_International_Airport" title="Ninoy Aquino International Airport">Ninoy Aquino International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clark_International_Airport" title="Clark International Airport">Clark International Airport</a>.</p>
<p>In 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine ranked Manila the world's most congested city. According to <a href="/wiki/Waze" title="Waze">Waze</a>'s 2015 "Global Driver Satisfaction Index", Manila is the town with the worst traffic worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> Manila is notorious for its frequent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traffic_jam" title="Traffic jam">traffic jams</a> and high densities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> The government has undertaken several projects to alleviate the traffic in the city. Some of the projects include: the proposed construction of a new viaduct or underpass at the intersection of España Boulevard and Lacson Avenue,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> the construction of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_Manila_Skyway#Stage_3" title="Metro Manila Skyway">Metro Manila Skyway Stage 3</a>, the proposed <a href="/wiki/Manila_Light_Rail_Transit_System_Line_2" title="Manila Light Rail Transit System Line 2">LRT Line 2</a> West Extension Project from <a href="/wiki/Recto_Avenue" title="Recto Avenue">Recto Avenue</a> to Tondo or the Port Area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> and the expansion and widening of several national and local roads. However, such projects have yet to make any meaningful impact, and the traffic jams and congestion continue unabated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Metro_Manila_Dream_Plan" title="Metro Manila Dream Plan">Metro Manila Dream Plan</a>, formulated in the mid-2010s seeks to address these problems. It consists of a list of short term priority projects and medium to long term infrastructure projects that will last up to 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_and_electricity">Water and electricity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Water and electricity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Water services used to be provided by the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Waterworks_and_Sewerage_System" title="Metropolitan Waterworks and Sewerage System">Metropolitan Waterworks and Sewerage System</a>, which served 30% of the city with most other sewage being directly dumped into storm drains, septic tanks, or open canals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> MWSS was <a href="/wiki/Water_privatization_in_Metro_Manila" title="Water privatization in Metro Manila">privatized in 1997</a>, which split the water <a href="/wiki/Concession_(contract)" title="Concession (contract)">concession</a> into the east and west zones. The <a href="/wiki/Maynilad_Water_Services" title="Maynilad Water Services">Maynilad Water Services</a> took over the west zone of which Manila is a part. It now provides the supply and delivery of potable water and sewerage system in Manila,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> but it does not provide service to the southeastern part of the city which belongs to the east zone that is served by <a href="/wiki/Manila_Water" title="Manila Water">Manila Water</a>. Electric services are provided by <a href="/wiki/Meralco" title="Meralco">Meralco</a>, the sole electric power distributor in Metro Manila.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Metro_Manila" title="List of hospitals in Metro Manila">List of hospitals in Metro Manila</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Philippine_General_Hospital.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Philippine_General_Hospital.JPG/220px-Philippine_General_Hospital.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Philippine_General_Hospital.JPG/330px-Philippine_General_Hospital.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Philippine_General_Hospital.JPG/440px-Philippine_General_Hospital.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Philippine_General_Hospital.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Philippine_General_Hospital" title="Philippine General Hospital">Philippine General Hospital</a>, the largest medical center and the national referral center for health in the Philippines.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Manila Health Department is responsible for the planning and implementation of the health care programs provided by the city government. It operates 59 health centers and six city-run hospitals, which are free of charge for the city's constituents. The six public city-run hospitals are the <a href="/wiki/Ospital_ng_Maynila_Medical_Center" title="Ospital ng Maynila Medical Center">Ospital ng Maynila Medical Center</a>, Ospital ng Sampaloc, Gat Andres Bonifacio Memorial Medical Center, Ospital ng Tondo, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Hospital_(Manila)" title="Santa Ana Hospital (Manila)">Sta. Ana Hospital</a>, and Justice Jose Abad Santos General Hospital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> Manila is also the site of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_General_Hospital" title="Philippine General Hospital">Philippine General Hospital</a>, the tertiary state-owned hospital administered and operated by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines_Manila" title="University of the Philippines Manila">University of the Philippines Manila</a>. The city is also planning to put up an education, research and hospital facility for <a href="/wiki/Cleft_lip_and_cleft_palate" title="Cleft lip and cleft palate">cleft-palate</a> patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manila's healthcare is also provided by private corporations. Private hospitals that operates in the city are the Manila Doctors Hospital, Chinese General Hospital and Medical Center, Dr. José R. Reyes Memorial Medical Center, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Medical_Center" title="Metropolitan Medical Center">Metropolitan Medical Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_Hospital_(Manila)" title="Our Lady of Lourdes Hospital (Manila)">Our Lady of Lourdes Hospital</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas_Hospital" title="University of Santo Tomas Hospital">University of Santo Tomas Hospital</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health_(Philippines)" title="Department of Health (Philippines)">Department of Health</a> has its main office in Manila. The national health department also operates the San Lazaro Hospital, a special referral tertiary hospital. Manila is also the home to the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>'s Regional Office for the Western Pacific and Country Office for the Philippines.</p>
<p>The city has free immunization programs for children, specifically targeted against the seven major diseases – smallpox, diphtheria, tetanus, yellow fever, whooping cough, polio, and measles. As of 2016, a total of 31,115 children age one and below has been “fully immunized”.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> The Manila Dialysis Center that provides free services for the poor has been cited by the United Nations Committee on Innovation, Competitiveness and Public-Private Partnerships as a model for public-private partnership (PPP) projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_universities_and_colleges_in_Manila" title="List of universities and colleges in Manila">List of universities and colleges in Manila</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_of_City_Schools%E2%80%93Manila" title="Division of City Schools–Manila">Division of City Schools–Manila</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St._La_Salle_Hall_Facade.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1938" data-file-width="2580" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/St._La_Salle_Hall_Facade.JPG/220px-St._La_Salle_Hall_Facade.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/St._La_Salle_Hall_Facade.JPG/330px-St._La_Salle_Hall_Facade.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/St._La_Salle_Hall_Facade.JPG/440px-St._La_Salle_Hall_Facade.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St._La_Salle_Hall_Facade.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/De_La_Salle_University" title="De La Salle University">De La Salle University</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Lasallian_educational_institutions" title="Lasallian educational institutions">Lasallian educational institution</a> established in 1911.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="402" data-file-width="600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg/220px-Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg/330px-Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg/440px-Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_City_of_Manila" title="University of the City of Manila">University of the City of Manila</a> and Baluarte de San Diego in <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UST-gardensjf.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/UST-gardensjf.JPG/220px-UST-gardensjf.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/UST-gardensjf.JPG/330px-UST-gardensjf.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/UST-gardensjf.JPG/440px-UST-gardensjf.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UST-gardensjf.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas" title="University of Santo Tomas">University of Santo Tomas</a> is the oldest existing university in Asia, established in 1611.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The center of education since the colonial period, Manila — particularly Intramuros — is home to several Philippine universities and colleges as well as its oldest ones. It served as the home of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas" title="University of Santo Tomas">University of Santo Tomas</a> (1611), <a href="/wiki/Colegio_de_San_Juan_de_Letran" title="Colegio de San Juan de Letran">Colegio de San Juan de Letran</a> (1620), <a href="/wiki/Ateneo_de_Manila_University" title="Ateneo de Manila University">Ateneo de Manila University</a> (1859), <a href="/wiki/Lyceum_of_the_Philippines_University" title="Lyceum of the Philippines University">Lyceum of the Philippines University</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mapua_Institute_of_Technology" title="Mapua Institute of Technology">Mapua Institute of Technology</a>. Only <a href="/wiki/Colegio_de_San_Juan_de_Letran" title="Colegio de San Juan de Letran">Colegio de San Juan de Letran</a> (1620) remains at Intramuros; the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas" title="University of Santo Tomas">University of Santo Tomas</a> transferred to a new campus at Sampaloc in 1927, and Ateneo left Intramuros for Loyola Heights, Quezon City (while still retaining "de Manila" in its name) in 1952.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_City_of_Manila" title="University of the City of Manila">University of the City of Manila</a> (Pamantasan ng Lungsod ng Maynila) located at Intramuros, and <a href="/wiki/Universidad_de_Manila" title="Universidad de Manila">Universidad de Manila</a> located just outside the walled city, are both owned and operated by the Manila city government. The national government controls the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines_Manila" title="University of the Philippines Manila">University of the Philippines Manila</a>, the oldest of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines" title="University of the Philippines">University of the Philippines</a> constituent universities and the center of health sciences education in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> The city is also the site of the main campus of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polytechnic_University_of_the_Philippines_Santa_Mesa" title="Polytechnic University of the Philippines Santa Mesa">Polytechnic University of the Philippines</a>, the largest university in the country in terms of student population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_Belt" title="University Belt">University Belt</a> refers to the area where there is a high concentration or a cluster of colleges and universities in the city and it is commonly understood as the one where the San Miguel, Quiapo and Sampaloc districts meet. Generally, it includes the western end of España Boulevard, Nicanor Reyes St. (formerly Morayta St.), the eastern end of Claro M. Recto Avenue (formerly Azcarraga), Legarda Avenue, Mendiola Street, and the different side streets. Each of the colleges and universities found here are at a short walking distance of each other. Another cluster of colleges lies along the southern bank of the Pasig River, mostly at the Intramuros and Ermita districts, and still a smaller cluster is found at the southernmost part of Malate near the border with Pasay such as the private co-educational institution of <a href="/wiki/De_La_Salle_University" title="De La Salle University">De La Salle University</a>, the largest of all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De_La_Salle_University_System" title="De La Salle University System">De La Salle University System</a> of schools.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_of_City_Schools%E2%80%93Manila" title="Division of City Schools–Manila">Division of the City Schools of Manila</a>, a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Education_(Philippines)" title="Department of Education (Philippines)">Department of Education</a>, refers to the city's three-tier public education system. It governs the 71 public elementary schools, 32 public high schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city also contains the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Science_High_School" title="Manila Science High School">Manila Science High School</a>, the pilot science high school of the Philippines.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_sister_cities_in_the_Philippines" title="List of sister cities in the Philippines">List of sister cities in the Philippines</a></div>

<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Barrows, David (2014). <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/38269/38269-h/38269-h.htm#pb139" rel="nofollow">"A History of the Philippines"</a>. <i>Guttenburg Free Online E-books</i>. <b>1</b>: 179. <q>Within the walls, there were some six hundred houses of a private nature, most of them built of stone and tile, and an equal number outside in the suburbs, or "arrabales," all occupied by Spaniards ("todos son vivienda y poblacion de los Españoles"). This gives some twelve hundred Spanish families or establishments, exclusive of the religious, who in Manila numbered at least one hundred and fifty, the garrison, at certain times, about four hundred trained Spanish soldiers who had seen service in Holland and the Low Countries, and the official classes.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Guttenburg+Free+Online+E-books&amp;rft.atitle=A+History+of+the+Philippines&amp;rft.volume=1&amp;rft.pages=179&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft.aulast=Barrows&amp;rft.aufirst=David&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gutenberg.org%2Ffiles%2F38269%2F38269-h%2F38269-h.htm%23pb139&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AManila"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"In 1637 the military force maintained in the islands consisted of one thousand seven hundred and two Spaniards and one hundred and forty Indians." ~<i>Memorial de D. Juan Grau y Monfalcon, Procurador General de las Islas Filipinas, Docs. Inéditos del Archivo de Indias, vi, p. 425.</i> "In 1787 the garrison at Manila consisted of one regiment of Mexicans comprising one thousand three hundred men, two artillery companies of eighty men each, three cavalry companies of fifty men each." <i>La Pérouse, ii, p. 368.</i></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Barrows, David (2014). <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/38269/38269-h/38269-h.htm#pb139" rel="nofollow">"A History of the Philippines"</a>. <i>Guttenburg Free Online E-books</i>. <b>1</b>: 229. <q>Reforms under General Arandía.—The demoralization and misery with which Obando's rule closed were relieved somewhat by the capable government of Arandía, who succeeded him. Arandía was one of the few men of talent, energy, and integrity who stood at the head of affairs in these islands during two centuries. He reformed the greatly disorganized military force, establishing what was known as the "Regiment of the King," <b>made up very largely of Mexican soldiers</b>. He also formed a corps of artillerists composed of Filipinos. These were regular troops, who received from Arandía sufficient pay to enable them to live decently and like an army.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Guttenburg+Free+Online+E-books&amp;rft.atitle=A+History+of+the+Philippines&amp;rft.volume=1&amp;rft.pages=229&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft.aulast=Barrows&amp;rft.aufirst=David&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gutenberg.org%2Ffiles%2F38269%2F38269-h%2F38269-h.htm%23pb139&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AManila"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Metro_Manila" title="Metro Manila">National Capital Region</a></td>
<td style="text-align:right;">2,936,116</td>

<b>†</b> See: <a href="/wiki/Positions_on_Jerusalem" title="Positions on Jerusalem">Positions on Jerusalem</a>. Both Israel and Palestinians claim Jerusalem as capital. <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> contains the Israeli parliament and almost all Israeli government ministries. <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> contains most foreign embassies in Israel; <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is the administrative seat of the Palestinian Authority.</div>

<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/1986_Asian_Winter_Games" title="1986 Asian Winter Games">1986</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/1990_Asian_Winter_Games" title="1990 Asian Winter Games">1990</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/1996_Asian_Winter_Games" title="1996 Asian Winter Games">1996</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Harbin" title="Harbin">Harbin</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/1999_Asian_Winter_Games" title="1999 Asian Winter Games">1999</a>:</b> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gangwon_Province_(South_Korea)" title="Gangwon Province (South Korea)">Kangwon</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/2003_Asian_Winter_Games" title="2003 Asian Winter Games">2003</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Aomori,_Aomori" title="Aomori, Aomori">Aomori</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/2007_Asian_Winter_Games" title="2007 Asian Winter Games">2007</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Changchun" title="Changchun">Changchun</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/2011_Asian_Winter_Games" title="2011 Asian Winter Games">2011</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Astana" title="Astana">Astana</a>-<a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/2017_Asian_Winter_Games" title="2017 Asian Winter Games">2017</a>:</b> <i><a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a></i></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
